GT Equivalence Verification (CRK6)
============================================================
GT: -c0*A*exp(-c1*_s*t) + c2*_m*sin(sqrt(A))
Candidates evaluated: 50
Matched candidate IDs: []
Matched candidates: []

I need to determine which candidates can exactly match the ground truth:

**GT: `-0.4466*A*exp(-0.08660*t) + 0.9910*sin(sqrt(A))`**

The GT has two terms:
1. A term proportional to `A*exp(-0.08660*t)` (exponential decay in t, linear in A)
2. A term proportional to `sin(sqrt(A))` (a transcendental function of A)

The key challenge is that `sin(sqrt(A))` is a very specific transcendental function. No finite combination of polynomials, exponentials of A, logarithms, power functions `A^c`, or rational functions of A can exactly equal `sin(sqrt(A))` for all A ≥ 0.

Let me check each candidate for the presence of `sin(sqrt(A))` or an equivalent:

**Candidates with trigonometric functions:**
- **Candidate 17**: has `cos(A*c9)` — this is `cos(c9*A)`, not `sin(sqrt(A))`. These are fundamentally different functions. [NO MATCH]
- **Candidate 41**: has `cos(A*c7)` with a `t` multiplier — `c6*t*cos(A*c7)`. The t-dependence can't be zeroed without losing the term. And `cos(c*A) ≠ sin(sqrt(A))`. [NO MATCH]
- **Candidate 42**: has `c6*sin(A*c7 + c8)` — this is `sin(c7*A + c8)`, not `sin(sqrt(A))`. The argument is linear in A, not sqrt(A). [NO MATCH]
- **Candidate 43**: has `cos(A*c8)` — same issue as 17. [NO MATCH]

**All other candidates** use combinations of: polynomials in A, `A^c` (power functions), `exp(c*t)`, `exp(A*c)`, `log(A*c+1)`, `log(A^c*c+1)`, rational functions, `Max(0,A)`, and `sqrt(A)`. None of these basis functions can produce `sin(sqrt(A))`.

- `log(c*exp(A*c) + 1)` (Candidate 45) is a softplus-like function, not sin(sqrt(A)).
- `A^c` for fractional c gives power functions, not oscillatory/trigonometric behavior.
- `log(A*c + 1)` is logarithmic, not sinusoidal.
- Rational functions like `c/(A^c + c)` or `A^c*c/(A^c + c)` are bounded rational expressions.

None of these can reproduce `sin(sqrt(A))` exactly. The function `sin(sqrt(A))` has specific oscillatory behavior (with decreasing frequency as A increases) that cannot be matched by any of these basis functions.

Let me verify candidates 42 more carefully: `sin(A*c7 + c8)` — could we set c7 = 0? Then sin(c8) is just a constant, and we'd need a constant to match `sin(sqrt(A))` which varies with A. No.

**Candidate 21** is complex but only involves `sqrt(A)`, `A^c0`, polynomials, and `exp(c6*t)` — no sin function. [NO MATCH]

After careful analysis, **none** of the candidates contain `sin(sqrt(A))` or any equivalent trigonometric function with a sqrt argument. The candidates with trig functions have `sin(c*A)` or `cos(c*A)`, which are fundamentally different from `sin(sqrt(A))`.
